## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (forced/damped oscillator ODE modeling)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is the time-derivative of velocity (acceleration), which is typically modeled by an ODE dv_dt = f(t, v) in oscillator theory and nonlinear dynamics. With only t and v available (no position), common identifiable structures include damping/drag terms in v and explicit time-periodic forcing or parametric modulation in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Constant acceleration (bias): dv_dt = c0 (constant offset/actuation bias)
- Linear viscous damping / linear stability: dv_dt = c0 + c1 * v (first-order local model near an equilibrium in velocity)
- Pure viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * v (velocity-proportional dissipation when no explicit forcing is modeled)
- Cubic nonlinearity in velocity: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 (odd-power nonlinear drag or normal-form truncation)
- Quadratic drag (speed-dependent): dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * Abs(v) * v (aerodynamic/turbulent-like drag in a 1D velocity ODE)
- Saturating effective damping/acceleration: dv_dt = c0 * v / (1 + c1 * v**2) (bounded acceleration response at large |v|)
- Pure harmonic drive (explicit forcing): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) (externally driven oscillator expressed as acceleration input)
- Driven + linear damping: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) - c2 * v (standard driven-damped first-order surrogate in velocity)
- Time-periodic (parametric) modulation of damping/gain: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * v (parametric excitation or time-varying dissipation)
- Limit-cycle normal form in velocity (Hopf-type in v): dv_dt = (c0 - c1 * v**2) * v (self-excited oscillation surrogate when position is unobserved)
- Driven limit-cycle surrogate: dv_dt = (c0 - c1 * v**2) * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (self-excitation plus external periodic forcing)
- Coulomb (dry) friction + viscous damping + drive: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) - c2 * sign(v) - c3 * v (stick-slip style dissipation with periodic input)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Term proportional to -v suggests viscous damping; the coefficient magnitude sets the decay time scale of velocity transients.
- Odd-power nonlinearities in v (e.g., v**3) typically encode amplitude-dependent dissipation or normal-form behavior near a bifurcation when only v is observed.
- Abs(v)*v indicates drag scaling with speed squared (direction set by v), often used as a proxy for turbulent/aerodynamic resistance.
- Explicit sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) in t is a signature of periodic forcing; c controls the forcing frequency seen in dv_dt.
- A product like cos(c*t)*v points to parametric excitation or time-varying damping/gain rather than additive forcing.
- Rational forms like v/(1+c*v**2) imply saturation (bounded acceleration) at large |v|, consistent with actuator limits or nonlinear dissipation.
- sign(v) terms indicate dry friction with a nearly constant magnitude opposing motion, producing discontinuities near v=0.
- Multiple harmonic terms sin(c1*t)+sin(c2*t) imply non-sinusoidal or multi-tone drive, often arising from nonlinear forcing waveforms.
- A nonzero constant term c0 in dv_dt can represent bias/gravity-like acceleration components or unmodeled steady inputs.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO25)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(v)
Candidate formulas: 58

GT is the fixed function
\[
0.938430539170744\,\sin(t)\;-\;0.866974142258927\,\sin(v).
\]
So any matching candidate must be expressible as “(constant)\(\cdot \sin(t)\)” plus “(constant)\(\cdot \sin(v)\)” with **no other dependence** on \(t\) or \(v\) (no polynomial/rational/exp terms in \(v\), no mixed \(t\)-\(v\) terms, no constants), and the \(t\)-sinusoid must be exactly frequency 1 (up to phase shift), and the \(v\)-dependence must be exactly \(\sin(v)\) (again up to phase shift in the argument, but it must be a sine/cosine of \(v\), not a polynomial in \(v\)).

A key structural obstacle: in the entire candidate list, **none** contains a term of the form \(\sin(v)\) or \(\cos(v)\). All \(v\)-dependence is via polynomials/rationals/exp/Abs/Max and sometimes multiplied by \(\sin(\text{something in }t)\) or \(\cos(\text{something in }t)\), but never \(\sin(v)\). Since \(v\) can be negative, we also cannot “fake” \(\sin(v)\) with \(|v|\) or piecewise Max terms.

Below I still check each candidate for whether all non-GT-like terms can be zeroed out and whether the remaining terms could match both \(\sin(t)\) and \(\sin(v)\).

---

### 1.
Has \(c3\sin(c4 t+c5)\) (can match \(0.9384\sin t\) via \(c4=1,c5=0,c3=0.9384\)).  
But all \(v\)-terms are rational/polynomial/linear and \(v\cos(c9 t)\) mixed. No \(\sin(v)\). Cannot match \(-0.86697\sin(v)\). **No**.

### 2.
Has \(c1\cos(c2 t)\) and also \(\sin(c5 t+c6)\) multiplied by \(e^{c4|v|}\) (mixed \(t,v\)). You can zero mixed term by setting \(c3=0\). Then you can match \(\sin(t)\) using cosine with phase shift, but remaining \(v\)-dependence is \(c0 v + c7 v^3 + c8 v/(c9 v^2+1)\), not \(\sin(v)\). **No**.

### 3.
Has \(c2\sin(c3+c4 t)\) (can match \(\sin t\)). Remaining \(v\)-terms are \(c0 v + c1 v^3 + c5 v^5 e^{c6|v|} + c7 v\cos(c8 t)\) (mixed). Can set mixed to 0 via \(c7=0\), and other \(v\) terms to 0 via coefficients, but then you have **no** \(\sin(v)\) term. **No**.

### 4.
Same issue as 3; \(v|v|\) instead of mixed trig, still not \(\sin(v)\). **No**.

### 5.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO25)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(v)
Candidates evaluated: 58
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the ground truth:

**GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(v) = 0.9384*sin(t) - 0.8670*sin(v)**

The GT has two terms: a sinusoidal function of `t` and a sinusoidal function of `v`. The key question is whether any candidate can represent `-beta*sin(v)` using its v-dependent terms and `F0*sin(t)` using its t-dependent terms.

**Critical observation:** The GT requires a `sin(v)` term. None of the candidates explicitly contain `sin(v)`. So I need to check if any combination of the v-dependent basis functions in the candidates can exactly equal `sin(v)` for all values of v.

The v-dependent functions appearing in candidates include:
- `v`, `v**3`, `v**5`, `v**7` (polynomial terms)
- `v/(v²+1)`, `v/(v²+1)²` (rational terms)
- `v*exp(c*v²)`, `v*exp(c*|v|)` (exponential terms)
- `v*|v|`, `v*cos(...)`, `Max(0,v)²`, `v**c` (other terms)
- `v/(|v|+c)` (rational with absolute value)

**Can any finite combination of these equal sin(v)?**

`sin(v) = v - v³/6 + v⁵/120 - ...` is an infinite Taylor series. 

- **Polynomials** (v, v³, v⁵, v⁷): A finite polynomial can never equal sin(v) for all v.
- **v/(c*v²+1)**: This is a rational function, not equal to sin(v).
- **v*exp(c*v²)**: This is an entire function but grows exponentially; sin(v) is bounded. No finite combination can work.
- **v*exp(c*|v|)**: Similar issue with growth rates and non-analyticity at v=0.
- **v*|v|**: This is v²*sgn(v), a non-analytic function.
- **v/(|v|+c)**: Rational function of |v| and v.

None of these basis functions, in any finite linear combination, can exactly reproduce sin(v) for all v. The function sin(v) is a transcendental function that is bounded and oscillatory, while all the v-dependent terms in the candidates are either polynomial, rational, or exponential in nature - none of which can reproduce the oscillatory, bounded behavior of sin(v).

Even combinations of these functions cannot produce sin(v):
- Polynomials diverge at infinity; sin(v) doesn't.
- Rational functions like v/(v²+1) decay at infinity; sin(v) doesn't decay.
- Exponential terms grow or decay; sin(v) oscillates.

No candidate contains `sin(v)` or any trigonometric function of `v`, so **no candidate can match the GT**.

Let me verify each candidate's verdict:

Candidates 1-58: All lack a `sin(v)` basis function. The v-dependent terms are combinations of polynomials, rationals, exponentials, and absolute values of v, none of which can reproduce sin(v) exactly.
